--- 帖子 #2222 ---
My experience is that stoch systems, especially TEB2, perform much better than MAs.

The problem I had when using TEB2 was that the slower stoch did not always show the trend correctly. During long steady trends the slower (e.g. 4H) stoch would indicate that trend is changing, but in many cases that was not true. So, instead of using stochs for determining the big trend, I moved to trendlines, like the graph shows.

I draw a trendline on the slower TF (e.g. 4H) and then move to a faster TF (1H) where I use stochs for entries.

But like you say, MA's can also be used for trend determination.

R

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #2223 ---
TEB2:

Stochs; 5.3.3 aand 14.3.3

charts: 4h and 30m.

Look for crosses on the 4h and draw a line when they occur. then move to 30m and when they cross enter. Stronger signal when they happen simultaneously (or as close as possible).

If you obey the rules it is difficult to lose. yesterday 21/09 I went long GBPJPY at approx 06:00 am GMT. 3 of the 4 crosses were in place and I said what the hell, the 4th is about to come. It did come finally half an hour later after I had been stopped for 35 pips. Had I waited for the 4th cross it would have netted me zillions of pips. So the moral of the story is that patience is a virtue.

Also the system is great if you can manage to follow the rules. Of course you can bent the rules a little if you feel it is going to happen. Yesterday it didnt happen for me but it does happen more often than not. I mean if I have the 3 out of 4 crosses in place i usually enter and end in profit.

Hope it helps.

Oh, I also use 4H channels, they are great and easy to find

TEB

--- 帖子 #2247 ---
Hi, see my comments below.

Someone also asked about hitting 30 pip SL's  even when the stochs show that is fine to enter. Notice that SL depends on the TFs you use. If you are using 4H and 30M, then imo SL should be bigger than 30 pips, I would suggest 60-80 pips.

But if you go down to 5M TF when you are opening (so you start from 4H, then 30M, and finally 5M), then you probably can cut SL to 20-30 pips.

Papertrade and test different SLs...

R

--- 帖子 #2249 ---
hey guess, it seems that you are pulling the trigger too soon. when the stochs cross on the 4hr, you should wait for the 30m to cross from the same relative position whether it be around or slightly above/below 20 or 80. for example, on your chart, you have the 4hr cross from around the 50. think TEB likes crosses below 50 and not to mention if they can be around the 20 even better. therefore, on the 30min chart, you need to be looking for the crosses at least below the 50 line of the stochs. the stronger moves tend to be closer to the the 20 line (and the 80 line in a downtrend). you can take those crosses that you have shown in your chart but those are low probability trades. you want to take the high probability trades.

i hope this helps. see if you can find the teb2 section and read up on it. its a lot i know to sift through, but it can be worth your while.

--- 帖子 #2264 ---
A couple of charts on euro. You notice that on 4H chart euro has broken the trendline, which means that now the 4H trend is down. If you try to use here 4H stochs they give a false indication that the trend would be up again after a short down period and you would be looking for longs instead of shorts... That is why i ended up using trendlines insteads of stoch for 4H trend.

So you go to 30M chart and identify stoch tops for shorting, and you notice that you could enter in three places. At least here that 30 pips SL would have been enough, but you could even go to 5M chart and look for an optimal entry point.

And when this new downtrend is forming up, you can draw a trendline when the first two tops are there and use the trendline for entries (when the price touches the line and stochs confirm that it is ok to enter). Remember to update the trendline whenever new tops (like in this downtrend) are formed.

R

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #2268 ---
Hey muyuam, the only advice I can give you is:

1. find out what time frames work for you. if you can sit at the computer all day, then maybe watching the 4hr, 30 system is good for you. if you cant, then try it out on different higher timeframes.

2. take only the best trades. wait for the stochs to line up at the correct levels and take those trades. be careful though, no system is 100% and sometimes you will suffer losses. just keep practicing until you have it down right and then practice some more to ensure you know it inside out. I am still testing my strategy but also testing others so I have not devoted the entire time to testing TEB2.

3. protect yourself always. use a stop loss!!

thats all for now, I am not that good in this system as yet, still practicing.

--- 帖子 #2269 ---
yes indeed. if the criteria is not met, SCRAP THE TRADE. it makes no sense chasing trades, more often than not you will lose. the market has a way of showing you what you want to see. actually, its not the market's fault, its ours. we see what we want to see at times rather than what is actually there. no need to run down the trades, just wait for the next time. patience is a virtue and in trading it means the difference between a profitable trader and a trader that loses constantly.

--- 帖子 #2276 ---
generally in an uptrend, you want the 30m to cross BELOW the 50 line and close to the 20 line if possible. You can take that trade as the cross is near the 50, however that is not a prime trade. if you were going to take that trade, possibly try with a smaller amount than you usually trade with.

with regards for exit and S/L those a difficult questions. you kinda have to figure out how much you are willing to risk and how much you want to profit. I personally use position sizing to properly calculate my risk and I like to put stops a little bit past areas of support and resistance. when the market moves in my direction, I am testing taking some profit and move the stop to breakeven so that I don't lose money. hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #2283 ---
hey guys, i found an indicator that could make teb style trading much easier. it is called 4tf stoch bars. this indicator is really nice. what it does is place the stoch readings from 4 time frames and display them as green and red (default)  up or down and thus makes it visually easier for you to see what is going on in several time frames by just viewing one time frame.

apparently what it does is take 4 successive time frames to display on the chart starting with the one that you put it on and then it goes up according to default mt4 tf settings. for example, if you put this indicator on the 15m, it will display 15m, 30m, 1h, 4h. if you place it on the 4h it will display 4h, D,W,M. so far as i know it is not customizable without some tweaking for custom time frames.

there are a few nuances with this indicator and I wanted to know if there is anyone who can help me improve this indicator. the biggest problem with this indicator is its repainting. lets say for example you place the indicator on the 1h and you have displayed 1h, 4h, d, w. lets say the 1h stoch is down and the 4h stoch is up. when the 4h stoch starts to turn down, it apparently will repaint the entire 4 hr bar represented in dots at times. for example, at some point the 4h is displaying green (up) when it switches about 4 dots will switch red. this can lead to false signals and can hurt traders. what i think should be done to improve the indicator is that whatever is the smallest tf displayed, all other boxes should be marked off at that regular time interval whether it be up or down. that way you won't have the higher time frames changing multiple dots, it will only change the most recent/current dot.

here is the indicator:
http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...2&postcount=24

i have tried PM'ing banzai and i am waiting on a reply but i think that if we can tweak this thing...it will be very helpful to a lot of traders.

what you guys think?

take care and happy trading.

--- 帖子 #2292 ---
Good to see the thread is still going. I'm still using TEB2, but I have 4 windows per each pair: 30min, 4hr, daily, and weekly. The reason for the 4 timeframes is that I can use combinations of different pairs for the same currency: 30min/4hr (the standard TEB2), 4hr/daily, daily/weekly. Also, sometimes I switch weekly with 5min to see the exact entry on 30min/4hr. The best trades of course happen when daily, 4hr, and 30min lign up (from TEB1), and by best trades I mean the amounts of pips, they are large when that happens. Once I had all of them ligned up, including weekly, on EUR/JPY, grabbed 120 pips and chickened out, but the pair kept falling for another 300 or so pips.

For the supp/res i use TL's, fibs, previous swing highs/lows; and also candlestick formations for reverse/retrace confirmation. I've given up on channels because I find previous swing high/low levels to give me more accurate results. And of course the stochs, when they lign up, we get the momentum.

Great system, thnx Teb.

--- 帖子 #2343 ---
Intersting web @ system I came a cross today

it works quite well

I would exit when the 5min crosses back

3 ducks system
http://captaincurrency.blogspot.com/

Firstly I would like to say, I did not reinvent the wheel with this system, I have just added one or two ideas to a 60 period simple moving average (sma) to make it my own and named it "The 3 Duck's Trading System" for obvious reasons as you will find out later on. The system is fairly straight forward and easy to use. Like a lot of trading systems it will be more productive when prices are moving in one direction and not stuck in a tight trading range. Of course this system has losing trade and losing runs, but with proper money management and good discipline I'm sure this system will keep you out of bad trades and give you a great chance to make profits in the Fx market. One of the nice things about this system is it will quickly tell you if prices are in an up or down swing phase and stop you from guessing! It will also allow you to decide to be a bull or a bear and trade in the direction of that trend. There are 3 charts involved in this system: a 4hr chart, a 1hr chart and a 5min chart. There is 1 indicator, a 60 period simple moving average (60 sma) plotted on each chart. There you go, its that simple.

How it works:

Step 1 - First Duck
http://bp0.blogger.com/_o93gCdxWKlc/.../4hr+cable.bmp

The first thing we need to do is look at our largest time-frame (4hr chart) and see if current prices are above or below the 60 sma. From this chart we can see that current price is below the 60 sma. This tells us that we maybe looking to sell.

Step 2- Second Duck
http://bp3.blogger.com/_o93gCdxWKlc/.../cable+1hr.bmpThe second thing we need to do is drop down to our 1hr chart. We need to see the current price below the 60 sma on this chart also, this gives us confirmation.

Important: If the current price was to be above the 60 sma on this chart we could not move on to step 3.

Step 3 - Third Duck
http://bp1.blogger.com/_o93gCdxWKlc/...5min+cable.bmpFrom step 1 and 2, current prices need to be below their 60 sma's on each chart. We are now on the 5 min chart and we are looking to sell when price crosses below the 60 sma. For extra confirmation we should let prices break the last low on the 5 min chart. This would mean that prices will be below their 60 sma on all 3 time-frames, therefore all 3 Ducks are lined up in the same direction.

Stop-Losses: This is where you can make this system your own. If you are a short term trader you may want to put your stop-loss above the highs on the 5 min or the 1 hr chart. If you are more of a positional trader you may wish to put your stop-loss above a high on the 4 hr chart. You could also use a fixed stop-loss, maybe 25-30 pips or more from entry. It all depends what type of a trader you are, so you decide! If you are a longer term trader or investor, this system can help you get a good entry point into the market. Another "trick" that may help you preserve capital, If you do sell and prices get back above the 5 min 60 sma by 10 pips (not a good sign) you may want to cut your losses short before your stop-loss. But if you are a longer term trader this may not be a big deal for you.

Targets: Same again, depends what type of a trader you are but target can be support or resistance levels.

Summary: The above example was carried out when the gbp/usd was trading lower so obviously we where selling - the system works just as well for buying opportunities, just look for prices to be above the 60 sma on all 3 time-frames, starting with step 1 again. I like this system a lot as it does not try to out-guess the markets movements and pick tops and bottoms. The system will quickly tell you to be a buyer or a seller. Its a good honest system that tries to follow prices. This system works better on currency pairs such as the Eur/Usd and Gbp/Usd, but there is nothing stopping you from plotting this system on any pair, but as we know some pairs act differently to others. The best time I found for trading this system is the European and US sessions. I lke to use this system as a guide in addition to my own market knowledge. Take care to watch what is going on around you - economic new releases, holidays etc.

by Captain Currency

--- 帖子 #2355 ---
I became familiar with the TEB system about a year ago, but never really got it going for me. But recently, I started fooling around with it as a longer term trade, using the weekly and daily charts. I guess it's more of a TEB 2 system. Anyway I have had very promising results backtesting several pairs from the first of this year till now.

The way I tested was like this. I determined the direction of the weekly and only took daily signals in that direction. On each signal that was generated, I took a one lot trade on the next candle that broke the high or low of the signal candle. I set a fixed stop at around 80 to 100% of the pair's Daily ATR depending on the pair, and set the limit at twice the stop. There were no add ons, no trailing stops, and no scaling out or taking early profits. Six pairs were tested. There were 64 trades, with 36 winners for a 56.3% winning percentage. The total profit was 6,025 pips. There was a fairly hefty 1,725 pip drawdown, the result of a stretch of ten losers in a row.

I think this is pretty exciting for a set it and forget it approach. Something to think about is that I used almost no discretion in these test trades. If it was a signal, I took it, no matter where the stoch cross occurred. A little discretion and some more logical stop and limit placement might produce a better winning percentage and a better return per trade, which by the way was about 94 pips average.

Is anybody else trading this method like this? I'd like to hear from and exchange ideas with those who might be, or even might be interested.

Cheers,

Richard

--- 帖子 #2357 ---
Red,

Hi. You're right about multiple time frames, but the basis is the use of stochastics as opposed to moving averages. You set up two different time charts each with two stochastic oscillators on them, and when the stochs are in agreement, that is all crossed in the same direction, you enter the trade. This a variation of the method first described at the beginning of this thread, but TEB 2 is formulated and discussed here as well. There are certain subleties to reading stochastics that are also discussed throughout this thread that you will find helpful. There is also a short thread on TEB 2 which gives the specifics--- http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=61902

Initially TEB 2 was designed to be a day trading strategy, but it seems to adapt well to a swing/position application. Take a look and see what you think.

Cheers,

Richard

--- 帖子 #2374 ---
In Metatrader 4 if you right click on the toolbar (say where the arrow or vertical bar icons are located) a menu will open.  If you click on "customize" it will enable you to add the regression channel icon to your toolbar.  This saves having to click on the INSERT|CHANNELS menu items.

The regression channel icon (it's labelled on the customize menu) is the single slash line with the hash marks across it.

--- 帖子 #2385 ---
My MTF MACD variant EA works pretty good - it has about a 2.00 profit factor and 75% winning trade percentage; however, it isn't very profitable and I'm sure that there are other EA's out there that are way more profitable.  The trick is that I'm not waiting for a MACD crossover, I'm using the MACD histogram and waiting to see if the current bar is either greater than or less than the previous bar.  It works good with H1 and M15 timeframes (and I'm combining it with ADX).

--- 帖子 #2409 ---
Hi Teb, good stuff, I've been using slow stochastics 14, 6 as my main indicator on about 6 timeframes. It spots trend peaks and valleys quicker than the MACD, but there is an art to it.

I use 4m, 20m, 1hr, 4hr, 1day, 1week, and I judge the trend by looking at the slow stochastics of each timeframe. It is safest when at least the 4 and 20 minute stochastics line up, but the more that are in sync the bigger the move that will occur in time so that one may let one's position ride if one chooses.

I use thinkorswim and just have like 6 chart snippets. I would suggest looking at the stochastics of all 6 to learn the process. It is an art because there is often a price peak or valley within overbought or oversold stochastics period which is the optimal entry point (rather than when it crosses above 20 or below 80).

I use real tight stops, .05%, which is like 5 pips. If I get stopped out I try to enter again real soon at a better entry, because it is even more overbought or oversold at this time. My exit is when the stochastics move to whatever extreme unless I feel the move is faltering and will come back on me, then I just exit at that time.

Right now I am using MACD, and ADX/DMI too, but am trying to streamline the complexity of my system down (which is still simple). I'll post my system and graphics once I get it stabilized. I am a relatively new trader and I find multiple timeframe trading using slow stochastics, MACD, or similar, to be the key to profitability. One can trade anything with this system too.

What system do you want to use

it depends on

1. on your time frames you want to trade

2. the amount of money you have

3. what tools do you like EMA, SMA CCI, STOCH etc

4. your risk level

5. all most all systems work - you must follow the rules.

take one my system and master it. they are all based on

1. multi time frames - which just helps you know you are with the trend on a few time frames.

2. helps you find great entries, and helps you find good stops and profits

ie.
4 hour: trend charts
1 hour: to find stops and profit

- Support and resistants and trend lines

- Round numbers -" 00" and "50" ie. 1.0250
15 mins: entry

cheers

--- 帖子 #2429 ---
The beauty of the system is once when you enter the trades you will exit only on 4hr stocs cross. That becomes your stop loss as well. So the stop loss will range from 10 pips to 40 pips, TP will hit from 20 pips to 200 pips, it is basically riding the intermediate wave in the 4hr chart in alignment with the major daily trend, 30 min is used for entry.

--- 帖子 #2433 ---
If you look at your chart, you'll see that MTF Stoch for D1 has crossed down on 13/4 at 00:00 whereas if you put a normal 533 stoch on D1 separately, you'll see that stoch crossed when daily bar closed. MTF shows daily stoch cross down when daily bar still open.

If the daily trend continues up or down, this is not a problem as you follow H4 and M30. But when Daily stoch crosses up or down, MTF indi always shows stoch cross when the daily bar is still open.

Of course, this is the case with H4 and M30 stoch crossing moments when using MTF stoch indi as stoch crosses happen when the bar is still open.

TEB explained how to tackle this as having experience with the indi and get a feeling for it when someone asked the same question.

I wonder how you are handling this. When you open a position in D1 direction while the bar is still open and all of a sudden price reverses and D1 stoch reverses and crosses back , what do you do or what are you planning to do if you haven't seen such a case yet?

Regards,

Blackeagle
